2020 ANNUAL REPORT CNPD Opinion relating to bill 7652 amending: 1° the amended law of 25 July 2015 on
creation of the automated control and sanction system; 2° the amended law of 14
February 1955 concerning traffic regulations on all public roads.

(Deliberation n°32/2020 of December 30, 2020)

In accordance with Article 57, paragraph 1, letter (c) of Regulation No. 2016/679 of April 27, 2016 relating to
the protection of individuals with regard to the processing of personal data and the freedom
movement of such data, and repealing Directive 95/46/EC (general data protection regulation)
(hereinafter “the GDPR”), to which article 7 of the law of 1 August 2018 on the organization of the Commission refers
national data protection system and the general data protection regime, the Commission
Commission for Data Protection (hereinafter referred to as “the National Commission” or “the CNPD”)
“advises, in accordance with the law of the Member State, the national parliament, the government and other institutions
and organizations regarding legislative and administrative measures relating to the protection of the rights and freedoms of
natural persons with regard to the processing”.

By letter dated July 21, 2020, the Minister of Mobility and Public Works informed the
National Commission for the preparation of a draft law in order to adapt the legal framework of the amended law of 25
July 2015 creating the automated control and sanction system (hereinafter referred to as "the amended law
of July 25, 2015) with a view to setting up “red light cameras”. As of August 20, 2020, the project
of law 7652 amending 1° the amended law of 25 July 2015 creating the control and sanction system
automated vehicles and 2° the amended law of 14 February 1955 concerning the regulation of traffic on all
public roads, was tabled in the Chamber of Deputies.

Not having been directly seized by the Minister, neither at the stage of the preliminary draft, nor at the stage of the draft
law, the CNPD nevertheless wishes to comment on draft law 7652, and on the interactions of the latter
with the legal framework relating to the protection of personal data. This self-assessment is explained by the fact
that the National Commission had already ruled on the bill creating the system
control and automated sanction and modifying the modified law of February 14, 1955 concerning the
traffic regulations on all public roads.

The bill under review is part of the “road safety” action plan (2019-2023) adopted by the
Government including various measures to be implemented by 2023 in order to combat road accidents
road and improve road safety. In this regard, the explanatory memorandum to the bill explains that “the measure
14 of this action plan provides for the strengthening of respect for red lights, in particular through the installation of
“red light cameras”. These radars are designed to detect non-compliance with a red light signal in a
systematic and automatic.

184 Opinion of the National Commission for Data Protection of 25 February 2015 (parliamentary document 6714/05).

228

52020 ANNUAL REPORT CNPDANNEXES In addition to speeding, as is already the case, and failure to observe a red light, as explained above, the
The purpose of the CSA system, in the longer term, is also to identify two other types of breaches of the Code of
the road, i.e. the failure to respect the safety distances between vehicles, and the fact of driving on lanes
reserved for other road users.

In this context, it is proposed to adapt the legal framework for speed cameras set by the amended law of 25
July 2015 with a view to setting up speed cameras to record these types of offences.

In this regard, the CNPD would like to share its observations on certain provisions of the bill.
presenting aspects relating to the protection of personal data, with regard to
in particular the installation of “red light” radars.

I. General observations on the legal framework

As a preliminary point, the CNPD notes that the bill proposes to modify article 3 paragraph 2 paragraph 1 of the law
amended on July 25, 2015 by providing for an extension of the consideration of breaches of the Code of
road by automatic speed cameras. If the latter only note for the moment the non-respect of the limitations of
speeds, they will also be required to measure: “1. The speed of vehicles approaching or moving away,
2. The average speed of vehicles between two points, 3. Failure to observe a red light signal, 4. The
distance from the vehicle in front corresponding to a travel time of at least two seconds,
5. The fact of driving on an emergency lane, a part of the roadway reserved for other users or a
lane closed. ".

The CNPD welcomes the government's choice to provide a legal basis for the installation of automatic speed cameras with
all of these features. It notes that such an approach has also taken place in a good number of
European countries. For example, in recent years, France185 and Belgium186 have installed
red light cameras along their roads and developed a legal framework to this end. The purposes of the installation
red light cameras in these countries are common to those of Luxembourg since they also tend to
reduce the driver's feeling of impunity and improve road safety. Red light cameras are there
generally installed in dense urban environments in order to ensure the protection of users in places
frequented by pedestrians, in cases where the action of crossing the road is particularly dangerous but also
especially in very busy areas.

II. As for the images taken by the red light radars

The CNPD observes that when noticing non-observance of a red light signal, depending on
the place where it is installed and the angle of the camera, a radar would be likely not only to capture the

185 In this sense, see the Order of 13 October 2004 creating the automated control system. As of July 1, 2017, 701 red light cameras were already
deployed. These figures can be found on the page https://www.securite-routiere.gouv.fr/radars/differents-types-de-radars/radars-fixes/radars-de-franchissement,
last accessed 11/18/2020.

186 In this sense, see the Royal Decree of 12 October 2010 relating to the approval, verification and installation of measuring instruments. Belgium, the 6th reform of
the State in relation to road equipment linked to road safety has provided the regions with powers relating to the crossing of red lights and to equip these
latest radars. Thus in Flanders, the Decree of the Flemish government of July 10, 2015 and in Wallonia, the Decree of the Walloon Government of June 21, 2018 come
modify the Royal Decree of 12 October 2010 mentioned above.

229

ANNUAL REPORT 2020 CNPD vehicle registration plate, photo of the driver, passenger, but also those of people
physical traffic on public roads, such as pedestrians crossing the road at this location. Depends on
configuration of the premises and the degree of use of the public space, a radar could therefore capture the images
faces other than those of the people present in the vehicle.

It is true that article 11, paragraph (3) of the amended law of July 25, 2015 provides that “during the financial year
of the right of access, anyone other than the driver is masked in the photo exhibited, unless the photo
relates to a vehicle used at the time of the offense in the context of learning or examination
practices for obtaining a driving license. However, this article does not mention the presence of
third persons on the images taken by the radars, such as possible pedestrians.

The CNPD therefore considers it necessary to automatically mask the images of pedestrians and any person
other than the driver, who would have no connection with the offence. In addition, the CNPD reiterates its questions, already
expressed in its opinion on the draft law establishing the automated control and sanction system and
modification of the modified law of February 14, 1955 concerning the regulation of traffic on all roads
public187, as to the relevance of limiting ourselves to masking third parties to the offense only when
the exercise of the right of access to the images of the driver or of the person presumed to be financially responsible.

It also considers it necessary to consider automatic masking of natural persons in the vicinity
roads that are taken during image capture, and temporary masking of vehicle passengers in order to
that they can be made visible again during any legal proceedings. A
such a mechanism would indeed appear to be more in line with the principle of data minimization provided for in Article
5 paragraph (1) letter (c) of the GDPR, which provides that personal data must be “(…)
adequate, relevant and limited to what is necessary in relation to the purposes for which they are processed
(…)”.

III. As for informing the public of the existence of red light cameras

The National Commission notes that the draft law does not mention informing the public of the existence of
these speed cameras at red lights. The CNPD recalls that article 12 paragraph 1 of the law of 1 August 2018 on the
protection of natural persons with regard to the processing of personal data in criminal matters
as well as matters of internal security provides for a minimum of information to be provided to persons
concerned. This article provides that “The controller shall make available to the data subject
at least the following information:

a) The identity and contact details of the controller;
b) The contact details of the data protection officer;

187 Opinion of the National Commission for Data Protection of 25 February 2015 (parliamentary document 6714/05), p. 4.

230

52020 ANNUAL REPORT CNPDANNEXES c) The purposes of the processing for which the personal data are intended;
d) The right to lodge a complaint with one of the two supervisory authorities referred to in Articles 39 and 40

and the contact details of said authority;

e) The existence of the right to request from the controller personal data relating to

a data subject”.

Paragraph (3) of the same article, however, provides that “the controller may delay or limit
the provision of information to the data subject pursuant to paragraph 2, or not to provide such
information, since and for as long as a measure of this nature constitutes a necessary and
proportionate in a democratic society, having regard to the purpose of the processing concerned, and taking due
account of the fundamental rights and legitimate interests of the natural person concerned, to:

(a) avoid interfering with official or legal inquiries, research or proceedings;
(b) avoid prejudicing the prevention, detection, investigation or prosecution of criminal offences;

matter or the execution of criminal sanctions;

c) protect public safety;
(d) protect national security and national defence; Or
(e) protect the rights and freedoms of others”.

Since the installation of automatic speed cameras at red lights concerns a much wider public
simply going beyond drivers and passengers in vehicles, the CNPD intends to attract
the attention of the authors of the bill on the obligation to inform all the persons concerned of
the existence of these speed cameras and the processing of data relating to them (e.g. signs informing drivers
and vehicle passengers as well as pedestrians at the locations of speed cameras installed at red lights). If it is considered
to limit or delay this information, the Grand Ducal Police would have to be able to justify this limitation or
delay of the right to information by one of the hypotheses referred to in Article 12 paragraph (3) cited above,
or even specify it in the text of the bill under consideration.

IV. As for the test phase of the installation of red light cameras

The National Commission understands that a first red light radar is installed in a very busy place in
Luxembourg-City, Place de l’Etoile for a test phase188. The Minister of Mobility and Public Works
also announces the effective installation of said radar around December 2020/January 2021 as well as the installation
additional 2 red light cameras in Hollerich and Schlammestee during 2021189. In
In this context, the National Commission considers that it is appropriate to take advantage of the test phase in order to observe whether
the installation of these red light radars raises questions in terms of data protection (as mentioned above).
above: do pedestrians appear in the images? are the persons concerned properly informed

luxembourg/a/1591684.html, last accessed on 09/12/2020.

CNPD 2020 ANNUAL REPORT of the presence of such radars, as developed in section 4 above? have some of them been

V. Regarding the exercise of the right of access to the data of the CSA system by the persons concerned

With regard to the right of access to data from the CSA system, the CNPD notes that the legislator has not taken
account of its position expressed in its previously mentioned opinion190. Indeed, Article 11 paragraph 1 of
the amended law of July 25, 2015 provides: "[...] the right to consult the photo of the offending vehicle
and the personal data relating to him processed in the context of the operation of the CSA system”.
Article 11 paragraph 2 provides that: “This consultation takes place at the Center and under the control of the Police.
grand-ducal”. In this regard, the National Commission once again wonders whether the obligation for the person
financially liable or the person named as the driver of the vehicle at the time of the offense
to move to the Center located in Bertrange, does not constitute an unjustified obstacle to the right of access of this
person  ?

However, this problem arises all the more following the entry into application of the law of 1 August 2018 relating to the
protection of natural persons with regard to the processing of personal data in criminal matters
as well as in matters of national security, of which Article 11 provides in its paragraphs (1) and (2) that:

“(1) The controller shall take reasonable steps to provide any information referred to in Article
12 and carries out any communication relating to the processing relating to Article 10, Articles 13 to 17 and
Article 30 to the data subject in a concise, comprehensible and easily accessible manner, in terms
clear and simple. The information is provided by any appropriate means, including electronically. Of
Generally, the data controller provides the information in the same form as the request.

(2) The controller shall facilitate the exercise of the rights conferred on the data subject by Article 10 and
sections 13 to 17”.

Article 13 of the aforementioned law provides that:

“Subject to Article 14, the data subject has the right to obtain from the controller confirmation
that personal data concerning him are or are not processed and, when they are, access
to said data as well as the following information:

a) the purposes of the processing and its legal basis;

190 Opinion of the National Commission for Data Protection of 25 February 2015 (parliamentary document 6714/05), p. 4.

232

52020 ANNUAL REPORT CNPDANNEXES b) the categories of personal data concerned;

c) the recipients or categories of recipients to whom the personal data have been
communicated, in particular recipients who are established in third countries or organizations
international;

d) where possible, the envisaged retention period of the personal data or, where

this is not possible, the criteria used to determine this duration;

e) the existence of the right to request from the controller the rectification or erasure of the data to
personal character, or the restriction of the processing of personal data relating to the person
concerned;

f) the right to lodge a complaint with one of the two competent supervisory authorities referred to in

Articles 39 and 40 and the contact details of the said authority;

g) the communication of personal data being processed, as well as any information

available as to their source.

In this context, since the entry into force of the amended law of 25 July 2015, the National Commission has
received numerous requests for information and complaints, from citizens wondering about the need
having to go to the Center in Bertrange to consult the photo of the offending vehicle, and thus
to exercise their right of access, which effectively raises the question of the compatibility of Article 11 of this law with
the aforementioned law of 1 August 2018.

In this regard, public petition no. 1216 “to obtain/send a copy of the photo
taken during an automated traffic control (Radar), even if it is true that this petition has not
obtained the required number of signatures in order to be the subject of a public debate.

Consequently, the National Commission reiterates its position expressed in the opinion on the draft law on
creation of the automated control and sanction system and modification of the amended law of February 14, 1955
concerning traffic regulations on all public roads. It therefore considers it necessary
to modify article 11 paragraph 2 of the amended law of 25 July 2015 in order to allow “[…] to the
financially responsible person or the person designated as the driver of the vehicle at the time of
the offense of consulting the photo concerning his vehicle, according to his choice, on site at the Centre, or of receiving
communication of the photo via a prior written request addressed to the Centre”.

233

ANNUAL REPORT 2020 CNPD VI. As for the retention period of the photos

The National Commission wonders whether, on the occasion of the introduction of Bill 7652, it would not be useful
to clarify the question of the retention period of photos taken from speed cameras, which it had already raised
in its opinion of 25 February 2015191?

The retention periods for recorded data are currently provided for in Article 4 of the Grand-
ducal of 7 August 2015 authorizing the creation of a file and the processing of personal data in the
framework of the automated control and sanction system192.

Moreover, article 2 of this same Grand-Ducal regulation indicates that the file contains only the data
“by observed and recorded infringement”. Should we understand a contrario that if there is no infringement found,
the photos are not saved and automatically destroyed?

Otherwise, it would be essential to provide in the Grand-Ducal law or regulation what happens
images from radars, whereas in the eyes of the CNPD, these should be immediately destroyed
in the event that no infringement is observed, in order to respect the principle of the retention period
limited data, provided for in Article 3 paragraph (1) letter e) of the aforementioned law of 1 August 2018.

Thus decided in Belvaux on December 30, 2020.
